$$f(t, P) = 0.4771 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.7761 \cdot t) + 0.4455 \cdot (1 - P/51.06) \cdot P + 0.4455 \cdot P$$

$$= 0.4771 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.7761 \cdot t) + 0.4455 \cdot P - 0.4455 \cdot P^2/51.06 + 0.4455 \cdot P$$

$$= 0.4771 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.7761 \cdot t) + 0.8909 \cdot P - 0.008726 \cdot P^2$$

So the GT is essentially:
$$f(t, P) = a \cdot P \cdot \sin(b \cdot t) + c \cdot P + d \cdot P^2$$

where $a \approx 0.4771$, $b \approx 0.7761$, $c \approx 0.8909$, $d \approx -0.008726$.

The key basis functions are:
1. $P \cdot \sin(b \cdot t)$ â€” a product of P and sin(t)
2. $P$ â€” linear in P
3. $P^2$ â€” quadratic in P

This is a **bilinear/polynomial** expression in P with sinusoidal modulation.

## Checking Candidates

Now I need to check if any candidate can produce exactly $a \cdot P \cdot \sin(bt) + c \cdot P + d \cdot P^2$.

### Key observations about candidates:

Most candidates have the form `P*c0/(c1 + t)**5 + ...` or involve `P**(1/4)`, `exp(P*c)`, `log(P*c+1)`, `1/(P+c)`, etc.

**Critical issue:** The GT requires a $P^2$ term and a $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ term. Let me check which candidates can produce both.

**The $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ term:** None of the candidates have an explicit $P \cdot \sin(...)$ term. All candidates have $\sin(c \cdot t + c)$ without P multiplied. This is a fundamental problem â€” $\sin(bt)$ and $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ are linearly independent basis functions. No amount of constant tuning can make $c_3 \cdot \sin(c_4 t + c_5)$ equal to $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ for all P.

**The $P^2$ term:** Most candidates don't have a $P^2$ term either. Some have terms like $P \cdot c/(c+t)^5$ which gives $P$ dependence but not $P^2$.

Let me carefully check each candidate for the possibility of generating $P \cdot \sin(bt)$:

Going through all 50 candidates:
- Every single candidate has $\sin(c \cdot t + c)$ as an additive term, NOT multiplied by P.
- The GT requires $P \cdot \sin(bt)$, which depends on both P and t multiplicatively.
- Since $\sin(bt)$ (function of t only) and $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ (function of both P and t) are fundamentally different â€” they cannot be made equal for all values of P.

No candidate has a term of the form $P \cdot \sin(...)$ or any mechanism to produce such a term.

Additionally, the $P^2$ term in the GT cannot be produced by any candidate either. Some candidates have terms like `P*c0/(c1+t)**5` which is $P$ times a function of $t$, but this doesn't give $P^2$. Candidates with `exp(P*c)` cannot exactly reproduce $P^2$ (exponential vs polynomial â€” linearly independent).

### Conclusion

The GT fundamentally requires:
1. A $P \cdot \sin(bt)$ term (bilinear coupling between P and t through sine)
2. A $P^2$ term

No candidate possesses either of these basis functions. The sine terms in all candidates are functions of $t$ only (not multiplied by $P$), and no candidate has a $P^2$ term. These are linearly independent basis functions that cannot be replicated by any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates.
